    §5.25 Pipeline Strip Self-SSIM Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — structural coherence SCANS fallback]¶

    Problem: Seams can pass the CGU, SC, FFT, Mono, SV, and Chroma gates yet still contain intra-strip structural jumps — strips that are internally inconsistent (top ≠ bottom half) signal a misaligned seam passing through a region with content.

    Implementation (shipped S175): - _strip_self_ssim(img, n_strips=8) in canvas.py: minimum NCC between top and bottom half of each strip; range [−1, 1]; near 1.0 = uniform; lower = seam cuts through strip - Stage 11.27: if ssim > _STRIP_SSIM_GATE_FLOOR (default 0.85) → SCANS fallback reason=f"strip_ssim_gate:{val:.4f}" - _STRIP_SSIM_GATE_ENABLED, _STRIP_SSIM_GATE_FLOOR; env: ASP_GATE_STRIP_SSIM, ASP_GATE_STRIP_SSIM_FLOOR - STRIP_SELF_SSIM_GATE_FLOOR: float = 0.85 in constants/animation.py - 5 tests in TestStripSsimGatePipeline (test_pipeline.py)

    §5.26 Benchmark Strip-SSIM & Chroma-Coh Metric Deduplication ✅ [Priority: Low — code hygiene]¶

    Problem: bench_anime_stitch.py had local duplicate definitions of _strip_self_ssim and _chroma_seam_coherence that diverged from the canonical canvas.py implementations.

    Implementation (shipped S175): - Removed local definitions in bench_anime_stitch.py; both functions imported from backend.src.animation.alignment.canvas - _compute_all_metrics() emits strip_self_ssim and chroma_seam_coherence from canonical source - 5 tests in TestBenchStripSsimChromaMetrics (test_bench_metrics.py)

    §5.29 Pipeline Ghosting SIQE Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — ghost artifact SCANS fallback]¶

    Problem: The existing GhostGate (§4.3) is a comparative bench gate only. The pipeline had no per-run ghost detection that could divert to SCANS without running the full bench comparison.

    Implementation (shipped S176): - _canvas_ghosting_siqe(img) in canvas.py — FFT autocorrelation of column-mean Sobel gradient; secondary peak at lag D in [5, H//4]; score 0–100 - Stage 11.28 in pipeline.py: fires when siqe > _SIQE_GATE_FLOOR (default 30.0) → SCANS fallback - Flags: _SIQE_GATE_ENABLED (ASP_GATE_GHOSTING_SIQE), _SIQE_GATE_FLOOR (ASP_GATE_GHOSTING_SIQE_FLOOR) - SIQE_GATE_FLOOR = 30.0 in constants/animation.py - 5 tests in TestSiqeGatePipeline (test_pipeline.py)

    §5.30 Benchmark Ghosting SIQE Comparative Gate ✅ [Priority: Low — bench ghost parity]¶

    Problem: Bench had no comparative SIQE ghost check analogous to the pipeline's Stage 11.28.

    Implementation (shipped S176): - GhostSiqeGate block after ChromaSeamGate in run_dataset() — reuses _ghosting_score_v2 - Fires when asp_siqe > max(_GHOST_SIQE_ABS_FLOOR, _GHOST_SIQE_RATIO_LIMIT × sim_siqe) - _GHOST_SIQE_RATIO_LIMIT=2.0 (ASP_GATE_GHOST_SIQE_RATIO), _GHOST_SIQE_ABS_FLOOR=30.0 - Schema entry ASP_GATE_GHOST_SIQE_RATIO in config.py - 5 tests in TestGhostSiqeGate (test_bench_metrics.py)

    §5.31 Pipeline Seam Band NCC Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — seam discontinuity SCANS fallback]¶

    Problem: A seam can be numerically coherent (SC gate passes) yet visually discontinuous if pixel content above and below the boundary have very different texture structure.

    Implementation (shipped S176): - _seam_band_ncc_min(img, n_strips=8, band_px=10) in canvas.py — minimum NCC between ±band_px bands above/below each strip boundary - Stage 11.29 in pipeline.py: fires when ncc < floor (LOW NCC = bad — inverted from other gates) - Flags: _SEAM_BAND_NCC_GATE_ENABLED (ASP_GATE_SEAM_BAND_NCC), _SEAM_BAND_NCC_GATE_FLOOR (ASP_GATE_SEAM_BAND_NCC_FLOOR, default 0.30) - SEAM_BAND_NCC_GATE_FLOOR = 0.30 in constants/animation.py - 5 tests in TestSeamBandNccGatePipeline (test_pipeline.py)

    §5.32 Pipeline Strip Gradient CV Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — sharpness consistency SCANS fallback]¶

    Problem: A stitched canvas can have strips of inconsistent sharpness — one strip sharp, the next blurred — indicating alignment/blending failures that no luminance-based gate catches.

    Implementation (shipped S176): - _strip_gradient_cv(img, n_strips=8) in canvas.py — coefficient of variation of per-strip mean Laplacian energy - Stage 11.30 in pipeline.py: fires when cv > _STRIP_GRAD_CV_GATE_FLOOR (default 0.50) → SCANS fallback - Flags: _STRIP_GRAD_CV_GATE_ENABLED (ASP_GATE_STRIP_GRAD_CV), _STRIP_GRAD_CV_GATE_FLOOR (ASP_GATE_STRIP_GRAD_CV_FLOOR) - STRIP_GRAD_CV_GATE_FLOOR = 0.50 in constants/animation.py - 5 tests in TestStripGradCvGatePipeline (test_pipeline.py)

    §5.33 Pipeline Seam Gradient Ratio Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — hard seam cut SCANS fallback]¶

    Problem: Stitched canvases can have hard luminance/gradient cuts at strip boundaries (visible as distinct horizontal lines), undetected by CGU or SC gates.

    Implementation (shipped S177): - _strip_seam_gradient_score(img, n_strips=8) in canvas.py — max ratio of boundary-row Laplacian gradient (±5px window) to middle-third interior gradient across all strip boundaries; capped at 10.0 - Stage 11.31 in pipeline.py: fires when ratio > _SEAM_GRAD_RATIO_GATE_FLOOR (default 3.0) → SCANS fallback - Flags: _SEAM_GRAD_RATIO_GATE_ENABLED (ASP_GATE_SEAM_GRAD_RATIO), _SEAM_GRAD_RATIO_GATE_FLOOR (ASP_GATE_SEAM_GRAD_RATIO_FLOOR) - SEAM_GRAD_RATIO_GATE_FLOOR = 3.0 in constants/animation.py - 5 tests in TestSeamGradRatioGatePipeline (test_pipeline.py)

    §5.34 Pipeline Canvas Aspect-Ratio Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — wrong scroll axis SCANS fallback]¶

    Problem: A canvas that is landscape (W > H) is almost certainly the result of wrong scroll axis detection (horizontal instead of vertical). The existing _detect_scroll_axis gate fires earlier, but this gate catches cases where the canvas grew sideways due to bad affine solutions.

    Implementation (shipped S177): - _canvas_aspect_ratio(img) in canvas.py — H/W ratio of the output canvas; portrait = correct; landscape = failure - Stage 11.32 in pipeline.py: fires when ratio < floor (LOW = landscape = failure); dynamic floor = max(_CANVAS_ASPECT_GATE_FLOOR, N * 0.3) - Flags: _CANVAS_ASPECT_GATE_ENABLED (ASP_GATE_CANVAS_ASPECT), _CANVAS_ASPECT_GATE_FLOOR (ASP_GATE_CANVAS_ASPECT_FLOOR) - CANVAS_ASPECT_GATE_FLOOR = 1.2 in constants/animation.py - 5 tests in TestCanvasAspectGatePipeline (test_pipeline.py)

    §5.35 Benchmark Seam Band NCC Comparative Gate ✅ [Priority: Low — bench NCC parity]¶

    Problem: The bench suite lacked a NCC-based comparative gate analogous to the pipeline's Stage 11.29; mismatched seam boundaries could pass all luminance gates but fail NCC.

    Implementation (shipped S177): - SeamBandNccGate block after GhostSiqeGate in run_dataset() — reuses _seam_band_ncc_min from canvas.py - Fires when asp_ncc < _SEAM_NCC_ABS_FLOOR (default 0.10) OR asp_ncc < 0.5 × sim_ncc when sim_ncc > 0.1 - Module constants: _SEAM_NCC_ABS_FLOOR=0.10, _SEAM_NCC_RATIO=0.5; schema entries ASP_GATE_SEAM_NCC_FLOOR, ASP_GATE_SEAM_NCC_RATIO - 5 tests in TestSeamBandNccGateBench (test_bench_metrics.py)

    §5.36 Pipeline Strip Histogram Intersection Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — color mismatch SCANS fallback]¶

    Problem: Color-step artifacts between strips (different color temperatures, saturation mismatches) that pass luminance-based gates but are visually obvious to the human eye.

    Implementation (shipped S177): - _strip_hist_intersection_min(img, n_strips=8) in canvas.py — minimum normalized histogram intersection (64-bin greyscale, cv2.HISTCMP_INTERSECT) between all adjacent strip pairs; 0=completely different histograms, 1=identical - Stage 11.33 in pipeline.py: fires when intersection < floor (LOW = color mismatch); default floor 0.35 - Flags: _HIST_INTERSECT_GATE_ENABLED (ASP_GATE_HIST_INTERSECT), _HIST_INTERSECT_GATE_FLOOR (ASP_GATE_HIST_INTERSECT_FLOOR) - HIST_INTERSECT_GATE_FLOOR = 0.35 in constants/animation.py - 5 tests in TestHistIntersectGatePipeline (test_pipeline.py)

    §5.37 Bench Histogram Intersection Comparative Gate ✅ [Priority: Low — bench color-mismatch parity]¶

    Problem: The pipeline's Stage 11.33 HistIntersectGate triggers a SCANS fallback when per-strip color distributions diverge. The benchmark has no corresponding comparative check to record when ASP's histogram intersection is worse than SCANS, so comparative analysis is blind to this failure mode.

    Implementation (shipped S178): - HistIntersectGate block in bench_anime_stitch.py run_dataset() after SeamBandNccGate - Fires when asp_hi < _HIST_INTERSECT_ABS_FLOOR (default 0.10) OR asp_hi < _HIST_INTERSECT_RATIO × sim_hi (default 0.5) when sim_hi > 0.1 - Module constants: _HIST_INTERSECT_ABS_FLOOR, _HIST_INTERSECT_RATIO; schema entry ASP_GATE_HIST_INTERSECT_RATIO added to config.py - 5 tests in TestHistIntersectGateBench (test_bench_metrics.py)

    §5.38 Pipeline Strip Saturation CV Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — color saturation mismatch SCANS fallback]¶

    Problem: Seam boundaries can induce color saturation mismatches between strips — one strip is vivid while adjacent strips appear washed-out. No gate catches this failure mode directly.

    Implementation (shipped S178): - _strip_sat_cv(img, n_strips=8) in canvas.py — coefficient of variation (std/mean) of per-strip mean HSV S-channel saturation; returns 0.0 for monochrome/degenerate input - Stage 11.34 gate in pipeline.py: fires when cv > _SAT_CV_GATE_FLOOR (default 0.40) → SCANS fallback - Flags: _SAT_CV_GATE_ENABLED (ASP_GATE_SAT_CV, default 1), _SAT_CV_GATE_FLOOR (ASP_GATE_SAT_CV_FLOOR, default 0.40) - SAT_CV_GATE_FLOOR = 0.40 in constants/animation.py; 2 schema entries in config.py - 5 tests in TestStripSatCv (test_canvas.py), 5 tests in TestSatCvGatePipeline (test_pipeline.py)

    §5.39 Pipeline Canvas Valid-Area Ratio Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — underfilled canvas SCANS fallback]¶

    Problem: When frame alignment fails catastrophically, the composite canvas may be mostly black (frames didn't overlap as expected). No gate fires on this underfilled canvas condition.

    Implementation (shipped S178): - _canvas_valid_area_ratio(img, black_threshold=8) in canvas.py — fraction of pixels with grayscale > threshold; low ratio = large black/empty regions; returns 1.0 for degenerate input - Stage 11.35 gate in pipeline.py: fires when ratio < floor (LOW = underfilled); default floor 0.55 - Flags: _VALID_AREA_GATE_ENABLED (ASP_GATE_VALID_AREA, default 1), _VALID_AREA_GATE_FLOOR (ASP_GATE_VALID_AREA_FLOOR, default 0.55) - VALID_AREA_GATE_FLOOR = 0.55 in constants/animation.py; 2 schema entries in config.py - 5 tests in TestCanvasValidAreaRatio (test_canvas.py), 5 tests in TestValidAreaGatePipeline (test_pipeline.py)

    §5.40 Bench Seam Gradient Ratio Comparative Gate ✅ [Priority: Low — bench hard-seam parity]¶

    Problem: The pipeline's Stage 11.31 SeamGradRatioGate triggers SCANS when ASP's seam gradient ratio exceeds the floor. The benchmark has no corresponding comparative gate to detect when ASP's seam cuts are disproportionately hard vs SCANS.

    Implementation (shipped S178): - SeamGradRatioGate block in bench_anime_stitch.py run_dataset() after HistIntersectGate - Dual condition: fires when asp_sgr > _SEAM_GRAD_RATIO_ABS_FLOOR (default 5.0) AND asp_sgr > _SEAM_GRAD_RATIO_LIMIT × max(sim_sgr, 0.1) (default 2.0×) — absolute floor prevents false positives on natural edge sequences - Module constants: _SEAM_GRAD_RATIO_ABS_FLOOR, _SEAM_GRAD_RATIO_LIMIT; 2 schema entries in config.py - 5 tests in TestSeamGradRatioGateBench (test_bench_metrics.py)

    §5.41 Pipeline Strip Hue CV Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — hue-shift seam detection]¶

    Problem: Seam-stitching can produce strips with inconsistent hue (hue shift across seam boundaries). No existing gate detects inter-strip hue inconsistency. The saturation CV gate (§5.38) catches saturation jumps but misses purely hue-shifted artifacts.

    Implementation (shipped S179): - _strip_hue_cv(img, n_strips=8) in canvas.py — circular mean hue per strip via cos/sin averaging (handles OpenCV 0–179 hue wrap); returns std/mean of per-strip mean-hue angles; returns 0.0 for monochrome (mean sat < 1) or degenerate input - Stage 11.36 gate in pipeline.py: fires when cv > _HUE_CV_GATE_FLOOR (default 0.50) → SCANS fallback - Flags: _HUE_CV_GATE_ENABLED (ASP_GATE_HUE_CV, default 1), _HUE_CV_GATE_FLOOR (ASP_GATE_HUE_CV_FLOOR, default 0.50) - HUE_CV_GATE_FLOOR = 0.50 in constants/animation.py; 2 schema entries in config.py - 5 tests in TestStripHueCv (test_canvas.py), 5 tests in TestHueCvGatePipeline (test_pipeline.py)

    §5.42 Pipeline Seam Boundary Sharpness Ratio Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — hard-cut seam detection]¶

    Problem: Hard seam cuts appear as unusually sharp rows at expected strip boundaries compared to strip interiors. The gradient ratio gate (§5.33) measures mean absolute gradient; this gate uses Laplacian variance — more sensitive to impulsive high-frequency edges.

    Implementation (shipped S179): - _seam_boundary_sharpness_ratio(img, n_strips=8, boundary_px=3) in canvas.py — Laplacian variance in ±boundary_px around each seam boundary row vs interior (middle half of each strip); returns max ratio across boundaries, capped at 50.0; returns 0.0 when interior_var < 1.0 to avoid degenerate flat-image false positives - Stage 11.37 gate in pipeline.py: fires when ratio > _SEAM_SHARP_RATIO_GATE_FLOOR (default 4.0) → SCANS fallback - Flags: _SEAM_SHARP_RATIO_GATE_ENABLED (ASP_GATE_SEAM_SHARP_RATIO, default 1), _SEAM_SHARP_RATIO_GATE_FLOOR (ASP_GATE_SEAM_SHARP_RATIO_FLOOR, default 4.0) - SEAM_SHARP_RATIO_GATE_FLOOR = 4.0 in constants/animation.py; 2 schema entries in config.py - 5 tests in TestSeamBoundarySharpnessRatio (test_canvas.py), 5 tests in TestSeamSharpRatioGatePipeline (test_pipeline.py)

    §5.43 Bench Canvas Valid-Area Comparative Gate ✅ [Priority: Low — bench underfilled-canvas parity]¶

    §5.49 Pipeline Strip Luma MAD Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — strip-level banding MAD detection]¶

    Problem: _strip_luma_range (§5.45) captures the extreme high-low span but is insensitive to systematic banding where multiple strips are shifted uniformly away from the global mean. Mean absolute deviation (MAD) of per-strip luma means provides a complementary signal focused on population dispersion rather than extremes.

    Implementation (shipped S181): - _strip_luma_mad(img, n_strips=8) in canvas.py — MAD of per-strip luma means from global mean; 0.0 for degenerate input - Stage 11.40 gate in pipeline.py: fires when _lmad_val > _LUMA_MAD_GATE_FLOOR (default 20.0) → SCANS; reason luma_mad_gate:{val:.2f} - Flags: _LUMA_MAD_GATE_ENABLED (ASP_GATE_LUMA_MAD, default 1), _LUMA_MAD_GATE_FLOOR (ASP_GATE_LUMA_MAD_FLOOR, default 20.0) - LUMA_MAD_GATE_FLOOR = 20.0 in constants/animation.py; 2 schema entries in config.py - 5 tests in TestStripLumaMad (test_canvas.py), 5 tests in TestLumaMadGatePipeline (test_pipeline.py)

    §5.50 Pipeline Strip Sharpness CV Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — mixed-frame sharpness detection]¶

    Problem: When composite strips come from frames with mismatched sharpness (e.g., motion-blurred frame stitched with a sharp frame), the per-strip Laplacian variance varies dramatically across strips. The coefficient of variation (std/mean) of strip Laplacian variance flags this without requiring a reference image.

    Implementation (shipped S181): - _strip_sharpness_cv(img, n_strips=8) in canvas.py — CV of per-strip Laplacian variance; 0.0 when mean sharpness < 1.0 (flat image guard) or degenerate - Stage 11.41 gate in pipeline.py: fires when _scv_val > _SHARPNESS_CV_GATE_FLOOR (default 1.0) → SCANS; reason sharpness_cv_gate:{val:.4f} - Flags: _SHARPNESS_CV_GATE_ENABLED (ASP_GATE_SHARPNESS_CV, default 1), _SHARPNESS_CV_GATE_FLOOR (ASP_GATE_SHARPNESS_CV_FLOOR, default 1.0) - SHARPNESS_CV_GATE_FLOOR = 1.0 in constants/animation.py; 2 schema entries in config.py - 5 tests in TestStripSharpnessCv (test_canvas.py), 5 tests in TestSharpnessCvGatePipeline (test_pipeline.py)

    §5.54 Pipeline Seam Chroma Jump Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — colour-step seam detection]¶

    §5.61 Pipeline Strip Entropy CV Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — scene-complexity mismatch detection]¶

    Problem: Strips from different frames can have very different information content — a complex background strip vs a flat sky or solid-colour cel region. High CV of per-strip Shannon entropy indicates composite segments from frames with mismatched scene complexity or strong background/foreground mismatch, which produces jarring visual discontinuities.

    Implementation (shipped S184): - _strip_entropy_cv(img, n_strips=8) in canvas.py — CV of per-strip Shannon entropy (256-bin luma histogram, -sum(p*log2(p+eps))); 0.0 when mean_entropy < 0.5 (uniformly flat guard) or degenerate input; high CV = information-rich strips adjacent to flat/uniform strips - Stage 11.46 gate in pipeline.py: fires when _ecv_val > _ENTROPY_CV_GATE_FLOOR (default 0.5) → SCANS fallback; reason entropy_cv_gate:{val:.4f} - Flags: _ENTROPY_CV_GATE_ENABLED (ASP_GATE_ENTROPY_CV, default 1), _ENTROPY_CV_GATE_FLOOR (ASP_GATE_ENTROPY_CV_FLOOR, default 0.5) - ENTROPY_CV_GATE_FLOOR = 0.5 in constants/animation.py; 2 schema entries in config.py - 5 tests in TestStripEntropyCv (test_canvas.py), 5 tests in TestEntropyCvGatePipeline (test_pipeline.py)

    §5.62 Pipeline Seam Chroma Step CV Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — inconsistent white-balance detection]¶

    Problem: Seam-stitching can apply white-balance normalization unevenly across composite zones, with some seams well-matched and others carrying large chroma steps. The §5.54 ChromaJumpGate detects the worst single seam; this gate detects inconsistency across all seams. High CV of per-seam chroma step (|ΔCb| + |ΔCr| in YCrCb) = unevenly corrected white-balance, which creates banding visible as alternating warm/cool strips.

    Implementation (shipped S184): - _seam_chroma_step_cv(img, n_strips=8, boundary_px=3) in canvas.py — CV of per-seam absolute chroma step (|ΔCb| + |ΔCr| in YCrCb space at ±boundary_px rows); 0.0 when mean_step < 0.5 (uniform chroma guard), fewer than 2 seams, or grayscale/degenerate input; complements §5.60 (luma step CV) and §5.54 (chroma jump max) - Stage 11.47 gate in pipeline.py: fires when _cscv_val > _CHROMA_STEP_CV_GATE_FLOOR (default 1.0) → SCANS fallback; reason chroma_step_cv_gate:{val:.4f} - Flags: _CHROMA_STEP_CV_GATE_ENABLED (ASP_GATE_CHROMA_STEP_CV, default 1), _CHROMA_STEP_CV_GATE_FLOOR (ASP_GATE_CHROMA_STEP_CV_FLOOR, default 1.0) - CHROMA_STEP_CV_GATE_FLOOR = 1.0 in constants/animation.py; 2 schema entries in config.py - 5 tests in TestSeamChromaStepCv (test_canvas.py), 5 tests in TestChromaStepCvGatePipeline (test_pipeline.py)

    §5.65 Pipeline Strip Chroma Energy CV Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — colour-palette mismatch detection]¶

    Problem: Strips from different animation segments can have wildly different colour saturation — a vivid cel-shaded character strip adjacent to a desaturated background or near-grayscale flashback scene. The §5.38 saturation CV gate uses HSV saturation; this gate uses YCrCb chroma magnitude (sqrt((Cb-128)² + (Cr-128)²)) which is more perceptually uniform, providing orthogonal coverage of the same class of defect.

    Implementation (shipped S185): - _strip_chroma_energy_cv(img, n_strips=8) in canvas.py — CV of per-strip mean chroma magnitude in YCrCb space; 0.0 when mean < 1.0 (near-monochrome guard), grayscale input, or degenerate; high CV = some strips vivid, others desaturated - Stage 11.48 gate in pipeline.py: fires when _cecv_val > _CHROMA_ENERGY_CV_GATE_FLOOR (default 0.6) → SCANS fallback; reason chroma_energy_cv_gate:{val:.4f} - Flags: _CHROMA_ENERGY_CV_GATE_ENABLED (ASP_GATE_CHROMA_ENERGY_CV, default 1), _CHROMA_ENERGY_CV_GATE_FLOOR (ASP_GATE_CHROMA_ENERGY_CV_FLOOR, default 0.6) - CHROMA_ENERGY_CV_GATE_FLOOR = 0.6 in constants/animation.py; 2 schema entries in config.py - 5 tests in TestStripChromaEnergyCv (test_canvas.py), 5 tests in TestChromaEnergyCvGatePipeline (test_pipeline.py)

    §5.66 Pipeline Seam Gradient CV Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — inconsistent blend-sharpness detection]¶

    Problem: Seam blending can be inconsistent across zones — some seams are hard cuts (steep gradient, 1-pixel transition) while others are gradually feathered (gentle gradient, 6-pixel ramp). High CV of per-seam mean absolute row-to-row luma change within ±5 rows of each boundary detects this inconsistency. Orthogonal to §5.60 (luma step CV) which measures total step magnitude; this gate measures transition steepness independently of step size.

    Implementation (shipped S185): - _seam_gradient_cv(img, n_strips=8, band_px=5) in canvas.py — CV of per-seam mean absolute row-to-row luma change in ±band_px rows; 0.0 when mean_grad < 0.1 (flat image guard), fewer than 2 seams, or degenerate; high CV = mix of hard cuts and feathered blends - Stage 11.49 gate in pipeline.py: fires when _sgcv_val > _SEAM_GRADIENT_CV_GATE_FLOOR (default 1.0) → SCANS fallback; reason seam_gradient_cv_gate:{val:.4f} - Flags: _SEAM_GRADIENT_CV_GATE_ENABLED (ASP_GATE_SEAM_GRADIENT_CV, default 1), _SEAM_GRADIENT_CV_GATE_FLOOR (ASP_GATE_SEAM_GRADIENT_CV_FLOOR, default 1.0) - SEAM_GRADIENT_CV_GATE_FLOOR = 1.0 in constants/animation.py; 2 schema entries in config.py - 5 tests in TestSeamGradientCv (test_canvas.py), 5 tests in TestSeamGradientCvGatePipeline (test_pipeline.py)

    §5.69 Pipeline Strip Luma IQR CV Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — tonal spread inconsistency detection]¶

    Problem: Strips from frames with very different scene content have different tonal spreads — a solid-colour action background has narrow IQR while a shaded indoor scene has wide IQR. The §5.45 luma range gate uses max-min of per-strip means; §5.49 luma MAD uses population dispersion of means. This gate uses IQR of within-strip pixel distributions (P75-P25 per strip), making it sensitive to within-strip content complexity rather than mean levels.

    Implementation (shipped S186): - _strip_luma_iqr_cv(img, n_strips=8) in canvas.py — CV of per-strip luma IQR (P75-P25 of pixel intensities within each strip); 0.0 when mean IQR < 1.0 (flat guard) or degenerate; high CV = wide-IQR strips adjacent to flat strips - Stage 11.50 gate in pipeline.py: fires when _iqr_val > _LUMA_IQR_CV_GATE_FLOOR (default 0.8) → SCANS fallback; reason luma_iqr_cv_gate:{val:.4f} - Flags: _LUMA_IQR_CV_GATE_ENABLED (ASP_GATE_LUMA_IQR_CV, default 1), _LUMA_IQR_CV_GATE_FLOOR (ASP_GATE_LUMA_IQR_CV_FLOOR, default 0.8) - LUMA_IQR_CV_GATE_FLOOR = 0.8 in constants/animation.py; 2 schema entries in config.py - 5 tests in TestStripLumaIqrCv (test_canvas.py), 5 tests in TestLumaIqrCvGatePipeline (test_pipeline.py)

    §5.70 Pipeline Seam Column Variance CV Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — horizontal step irregularity detection]¶

    Problem: A well-blended seam has a horizontally uniform luma step (each column transitions at roughly the same level). A partial registration failure or diagonal alignment artifact creates a column-wise step profile with high variance (some columns have large steps, others are flat). The CV of per-seam column variance scores detects when some seams have such horizontal irregularity while others are smooth — a sign that multiple different failure modes are active simultaneously.

    Implementation (shipped S186): - _seam_column_variance_cv(img, n_strips=8, boundary_px=3) in canvas.py — CV of per-seam variance of per-column absolute luma step (separate above/below row means per column); 0.0 when mean_var < 0.1 (flat guard), fewer than 2 seams, or degenerate; high CV = inconsistent horizontal regularity across seams - Stage 11.51 gate in pipeline.py: fires when _scvarcv_val > _SEAM_COL_VAR_CV_GATE_FLOOR (default 1.0) → SCANS fallback; reason seam_col_var_cv_gate:{val:.4f} - Flags: _SEAM_COL_VAR_CV_GATE_ENABLED (ASP_GATE_SEAM_COL_VAR_CV, default 1), _SEAM_COL_VAR_CV_GATE_FLOOR (ASP_GATE_SEAM_COL_VAR_CV_FLOOR, default 1.0) - SEAM_COL_VAR_CV_GATE_FLOOR = 1.0 in constants/animation.py; 2 schema entries in config.py - 5 tests in TestSeamColumnVarianceCv (test_canvas.py), 5 tests in TestSeamColVarCvGatePipeline (test_pipeline.py)

    §5.73 Pipeline Strip Luma Skewness CV Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — tonal character inconsistency detection]¶

    Problem: Anime strips can have fundamentally different tonal character — some dark with bright highlight tails (positive skewness), others bright with dark shadow tails (negative skewness). When the stitched canvas has strips with wildly varying skewness distributions, this signals tone-curve inconsistency or mismatched normalization that may not manifest as a mean-luma difference. CV of absolute per-strip skewness captures this orthogonally to §5.49 (MAD-CV, deviation magnitude) and §5.69 (IQR-CV, spread width).

    Implementation (shipped S187): - _strip_luma_skewness_cv(img, n_strips=8) in canvas.py — CV of |skewness| per strip (3rd standardized moment of grayscale pixel distribution); 0.0 when mean_abs_skewness < 0.05 (flat/gradient images), std < 1.0 guard per strip, fewer than 2 strips, or degenerate input - _LUMA_SKEW_CV_GATE_ENABLED (default ON) + _LUMA_SKEW_CV_GATE_FLOOR=1.5 in pipeline.py; Stage 11.52; env: ASP_GATE_LUMA_SKEW_CV, ASP_GATE_LUMA_SKEW_CV_FLOOR - Schema: ASP_GATE_LUMA_SKEW_CV (int 0/1), ASP_GATE_LUMA_SKEW_CV_FLOOR (float, 0–10); constant LUMA_SKEW_CV_GATE_FLOOR=1.5 in constants/animation.py - 5 tests in TestStripLumaSkewnessCv in test_canvas.py; 5 tests in TestLumaSkewCvGatePipeline in test_pipeline.py

    §5.74 Pipeline Seam Signed Step CV Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — alternating normalization direction detection]¶

    Problem: Gain normalization can produce alternating-direction brightness steps at seams (strip 0→1: brighter, strip 1→2: darker, strip 2→3: brighter). §5.58 (luma-step-CV) uses abs() on each step before computing CV, so uniform-magnitude alternating steps score near zero — they look "consistent" in magnitude even though the direction alternates. This gate uses std(signed_steps) / mean(|signed_steps|) which is high precisely when signs alternate.

    Implementation (shipped S187): - _seam_signed_step_cv(img, n_strips=8, boundary_px=3) in canvas.py — std(signed_steps) / mean(|signed_steps|) where signed_step = mean_above − mean_below at each seam; 0.0 when mean_abs < 1.0 (flat images) or fewer than 2 seams - _SEAM_SIGNED_STEP_CV_GATE_ENABLED (default ON) + _SEAM_SIGNED_STEP_CV_GATE_FLOOR=1.2 in pipeline.py; Stage 11.53; env: ASP_GATE_SEAM_SIGNED_STEP_CV, ASP_GATE_SEAM_SIGNED_STEP_CV_FLOOR - Schema: ASP_GATE_SEAM_SIGNED_STEP_CV (int 0/1), ASP_GATE_SEAM_SIGNED_STEP_CV_FLOOR (float, 0–10); constant SEAM_SIGNED_STEP_CV_GATE_FLOOR=1.2 in constants/animation.py - 5 tests in TestSeamSignedStepCv in test_canvas.py; 5 tests in TestSeamSignedStepCvGatePipeline in test_pipeline.py

    §5.77 Pipeline Strip Luma Kurtosis CV Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — bimodal structure inconsistency detection]¶

    Problem: Anime frames vary structurally — some frames consist of cel character against flat background (bimodal luma, high excess kurtosis), others are complex scene frames (near-Gaussian, low kurtosis). When the stitched canvas has strips with wildly varying kurtosis, it signals that the composition pulled from frames with different structural complexity — likely due to misaligned frame selection or failed fg/bg separation. This is orthogonal to §5.73 (skewness, 3rd moment asymmetry) and §5.69 (IQR-CV, spread width).

    Implementation (shipped S188): - _strip_luma_kurtosis_cv(img, n_strips=8) in canvas.py — CV of |excess kurtosis| per strip (4th standardized moment − 3 of grayscale pixels); 0.0 when std < 1.0 per strip, mean_abs_kurtosis < 0.1, fewer than 2 strips, or degenerate input - _LUMA_KURTOSIS_CV_GATE_ENABLED (default ON) + _LUMA_KURTOSIS_CV_GATE_FLOOR=1.5 in pipeline.py; Stage 11.54; env: ASP_GATE_LUMA_KURTOSIS_CV, ASP_GATE_LUMA_KURTOSIS_CV_FLOOR - Schema: ASP_GATE_LUMA_KURTOSIS_CV (bool), ASP_GATE_LUMA_KURTOSIS_CV_FLOOR (float, 0–10); constant LUMA_KURTOSIS_CV_GATE_FLOOR=1.5 in constants/animation.py - 5 tests in TestStripLumaKurtosisCv in test_canvas.py; 5 tests in TestLumaKurtosisCvGatePipeline in test_pipeline.py

    §5.78 Pipeline Seam Texture Ratio CV Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — texture complexity mismatch detection]¶

    Problem: When seams cross texture boundaries (e.g., detailed cel region above, flat sky below), the Laplacian variance ratio above/below the seam is large. In a well-stitched canvas, all seams should have similar texture ratios (either all matched or all different by similar degree). CV of log(above_var / below_var) across seams detects cases where some seams are well-matched in texture complexity but others cross hard texture boundaries — a sign of incorrect frame ordering or failed seam placement. Orthogonal to §5.66 (gradient CV, step magnitude) and §5.74 (signed step CV, direction).

    Implementation (shipped S188): - _seam_texture_ratio_cv(img, n_strips=8, band_px=5) in canvas.py — CV of log(Laplacian-variance ratio) across seam boundaries (±band_px rows); 0.0 when mean_abs(log_ratio) < 0.05, fewer than 2 seams, or degenerate input; uses cv2.Laplacian(band, cv2.CV_32F).var() per band - _SEAM_TEXTURE_RATIO_CV_GATE_ENABLED (default ON) + _SEAM_TEXTURE_RATIO_CV_GATE_FLOOR=1.2 in pipeline.py; Stage 11.55; env: ASP_GATE_SEAM_TEXTURE_RATIO_CV, ASP_GATE_SEAM_TEXTURE_RATIO_CV_FLOOR - Schema: ASP_GATE_SEAM_TEXTURE_RATIO_CV (bool), ASP_GATE_SEAM_TEXTURE_RATIO_CV_FLOOR (float, 0–10); constant SEAM_TEXTURE_RATIO_CV_GATE_FLOOR=1.2 in constants/animation.py - 5 tests in TestSeamTextureRatioCv in test_canvas.py; 5 tests in TestSeamTextureRatioCvGatePipeline in test_pipeline.py

    §5.81 Pipeline Strip Edge Density CV Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — detail-level inconsistency detection]¶

    Problem: Anime strips can vary wildly in edge content — a cel character strip has many edges, while a flat sky strip has almost none. When the stitched canvas has strips with wildly varying edge density, it signals that frames from different scene complexity levels were incorrectly interleaved or that bg/fg separation failed and introduced flat zones between detailed zones. Orthogonal to §5.50 (sharpness CV = Laplacian std/mean, measuring response amplitude) and §5.46 (seam edge density, a single seam-region value not a strip-wise CV).

    Implementation (shipped S189): - _strip_edge_density_cv(img, n_strips=8) in canvas.py — CV of Canny(50,150) edge pixel fraction per strip; 0.0 when mean_density < 0.005 or fewer than 2 strips; uint8 conversion before Canny - _EDGE_DENSITY_CV_GATE_ENABLED (default ON) + _EDGE_DENSITY_CV_GATE_FLOOR=1.2 in pipeline.py; Stage 11.56; env: ASP_GATE_EDGE_DENSITY_CV, ASP_GATE_EDGE_DENSITY_CV_FLOOR - Schema: ASP_GATE_EDGE_DENSITY_CV (bool), ASP_GATE_EDGE_DENSITY_CV_FLOOR (float, 0–10); constant EDGE_DENSITY_CV_GATE_FLOOR=1.2 in constants/animation.py - 5 tests in TestStripEdgeDensityCv in test_canvas.py; 5 tests in TestEdgeDensityCvGatePipeline in test_pipeline.py

    §5.82 Pipeline Seam Local Contrast CV Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — seam placement complexity inconsistency]¶

    Problem: Seams placed in high-contrast regions are harder to blend than seams in flat regions. When the canvas has some seams in rich-texture zones (high local pixel std) and others in flat zones (low local pixel std), the CV of per-seam local contrast is high — indicating inconsistent seam placement that may yield visible artifacts at some seams while others look clean. Orthogonal to §5.78 (texture ratio = above/below comparison of Laplacian var) and §5.66 (gradient CV = step steepness magnitude, not absolute contrast level).

    Implementation (shipped S189): - _seam_local_contrast_cv(img, n_strips=8, band_px=5) in canvas.py — CV of pixel std in ±band_px seam bands; 0.0 when mean_contrast < 1.0 or fewer than 2 seams - _SEAM_LOCAL_CONTRAST_CV_GATE_ENABLED (default ON) + _SEAM_LOCAL_CONTRAST_CV_GATE_FLOOR=1.0 in pipeline.py; Stage 11.57; env: ASP_GATE_SEAM_LOCAL_CONTRAST_CV, ASP_GATE_SEAM_LOCAL_CONTRAST_CV_FLOOR - Schema: ASP_GATE_SEAM_LOCAL_CONTRAST_CV (bool), ASP_GATE_SEAM_LOCAL_CONTRAST_CV_FLOOR (float, 0–10); constant SEAM_LOCAL_CONTRAST_CV_GATE_FLOOR=1.0 in constants/animation.py - 5 tests in TestSeamLocalContrastCv in test_canvas.py; 5 tests in TestSeamLocalContrastCvGatePipeline in test_pipeline.py

    §5.85 Pipeline Strip Luma P90–P10 CV Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — outlier-robust tonal range inconsistency]¶

    Problem: The per-strip P90−P10 luma spread is a robust tonal range that excludes the top and bottom 10% of pixels (noise and hard highlights/shadows). When CV of this spread is high, strips have wildly different outlier-robust tonal extents — indicating tone-curve inconsistency not captured by the full range (§5.45 = max−min, sensitive to outliers), IQR (§5.69 = P75−P25, narrower), or MAD (§5.49, median-centred deviation).

    Implementation (shipped S190): - _strip_luma_p90p10_cv(img, n_strips=8) in canvas.py — CV of (P90−P10) per strip; 0.0 when mean_spread < 1.0 or fewer than 2 strips - _LUMA_P90P10_CV_GATE_ENABLED (default ON) + _LUMA_P90P10_CV_GATE_FLOOR=0.8 in pipeline.py; Stage 11.58; env: ASP_GATE_LUMA_P90P10_CV, ASP_GATE_LUMA_P90P10_CV_FLOOR - Schema: ASP_GATE_LUMA_P90P10_CV (bool), ASP_GATE_LUMA_P90P10_CV_FLOOR (float, 0–10); constant LUMA_P90P10_CV_GATE_FLOOR=0.8 in constants/animation.py - 5 tests in TestStripLumaP90P10Cv in test_canvas.py; 5 tests in TestLumaP90P10CvGatePipeline in test_pipeline.py

    §5.86 Pipeline Seam Hue Shift CV Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — cross-seam white-balance hue mismatch]¶

    Problem: White-balance normalization applied inconsistently across seams can produce shifts on the color wheel (hue angle) that differ in magnitude from seam to seam. The existing §5.62 (seam chroma step CV) uses YCrCb Cb+Cr magnitude; this gate uses HSV hue angle (degrees [0,180]) which is orthogonal: a large chroma step in YCrCb can be saturation-driven without a hue shift, and vice versa.

    Implementation (shipped S190): - _seam_hue_shift_cv(img, n_strips=8, boundary_px=3) in canvas.py — mean hue per seam band (OpenCV HSV hue [0,180)), wrapped difference to [0,90]; CV of absolute hue shifts; 0.0 for grayscale, mean_shift < 1.0, or fewer than 2 seams - _SEAM_HUE_SHIFT_CV_GATE_ENABLED (default ON) + _SEAM_HUE_SHIFT_CV_GATE_FLOOR=1.5 in pipeline.py; Stage 11.59; env: ASP_GATE_SEAM_HUE_SHIFT_CV, ASP_GATE_SEAM_HUE_SHIFT_CV_FLOOR - Schema: ASP_GATE_SEAM_HUE_SHIFT_CV (bool), ASP_GATE_SEAM_HUE_SHIFT_CV_FLOOR (float, 0–10); constant SEAM_HUE_SHIFT_CV_GATE_FLOOR=1.5 in constants/animation.py - 5 tests in TestSeamHueShiftCv in test_canvas.py; 5 tests in TestSeamHueShiftCvGatePipeline in test_pipeline.py

    §5.89 Pipeline Strip Dark Pixel Fraction CV Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — tonal polarity inconsistency detection]¶

    Problem: Anime frames have dark outlines and backgrounds; some strips may be predominantly dark (dark scene, silhouette zone) while others are bright (sky, interior with lighting). When CV of the per-strip dark pixel fraction (luma < 64) is high, the canvas has alternating mostly-dark and mostly-bright strips — indicating incorrect frame interleaving or failed tonal normalization.     §5.90 Pipeline Seam Saturation Shift CV Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — cross-seam colorfulness mismatch]¶

    §5.93 Pipeline Strip Sobel Energy CV Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — gradient activity inconsistency detection]¶

    §5.94 Pipeline Seam Value Shift CV Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — max-channel brightness mismatch at seams]¶

    Problem: The HSV Value channel (V = max(R,G,B)) captures brightness as the dominant channel — distinct from luma (weighted average) and from saturation/hue. A seam between a vivid yellow region (high Value despite no luma mismatch due to green+red balance) and a dark region will show a large Value shift. CV of per-seam |V_above − V_below| detects inconsistent max-channel brightness matching across seams. Orthogonal to §5.86 (hue), §5.90 (saturation), and §5.58/§5.60 (luma = 0.114B+0.587G+0.299R, weighted average not max).

    Implementation: - _seam_value_shift_cv(img, n_strips=8, boundary_px=3) in canvas.py — CV of |mean_V_above − mean_V_below| per seam (HSV V [0,255]); 0.0 for grayscale or mean_shift < 1.0 - _SEAM_VALUE_SHIFT_CV_GATE_ENABLED (default ON) + _SEAM_VALUE_SHIFT_CV_GATE_FLOOR=1.2 in pipeline.py; Stage 11.63; env: ASP_GATE_SEAM_VALUE_SHIFT_CV, ASP_GATE_SEAM_VALUE_SHIFT_CV_FLOOR - Schema: ASP_GATE_SEAM_VALUE_SHIFT_CV (bool), ASP_GATE_SEAM_VALUE_SHIFT_CV_FLOOR (float, 0–10); constant SEAM_VALUE_SHIFT_CV_GATE_FLOOR=1.2 in constants/animation.py - 5 tests in TestSeamValueShiftCv in test_canvas.py; 5 tests in TestSeamValueShiftCvGatePipeline in test_pipeline.py

    §5.97 Pipeline Strip Median Luma CV Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — strip brightness location inconsistency]¶

    Problem: The median (P50) of each strip captures its typical brightness — robust to outlier pixels from noise, compression artifacts, or isolated highlights. When CV of per-strip medians is high, strips have different typical brightness levels (some typically bright, others typically dark), indicating tonal normalization failed to equalize median brightness across strips. Orthogonal to: §5.45 (full range = max−min, captures extent not center), §5.85 (P90−P10 spread, robust range not location), §5.69 (IQR = P75−P25, spread not center), §5.49 (MAD = deviation from median, not the median value), §5.89 (dark pixel fraction = threshold count not median).

    §5.98 Pipeline Seam Entropy Shift CV Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — cross-seam information content mismatch]¶

    Problem: Seams can cross information-content boundaries — complex detailed content on one side and flat uniform content on the other produces a large Shannon entropy difference between above and below the seam. When some seams have large entropy shifts and others have small ones, CV of these absolute entropy shifts is high — indicating inconsistent content complexity matching. Orthogonal to §5.61 (strip entropy CV = variation of entropy across strips, not comparison above/below each seam), §5.82 (seam local contrast = pixel std in seam band, not histogram entropy), §5.78 (Laplacian variance ratio, frequency response not histogram).

    Implementation: - _seam_entropy_shift_cv(img, n_strips=8, boundary_px=3) in canvas.py — Shannon entropy (base-2) of 256-bin histogram per seam band; CV of |H_above − H_below|; 0.0 when mean_shift < 0.05 - _SEAM_ENTROPY_SHIFT_CV_GATE_ENABLED (default ON) + _SEAM_ENTROPY_SHIFT_CV_GATE_FLOOR=1.5 in pipeline.py; Stage 11.65; env: ASP_GATE_SEAM_ENTROPY_SHIFT_CV, ASP_GATE_SEAM_ENTROPY_SHIFT_CV_FLOOR - Schema: ASP_GATE_SEAM_ENTROPY_SHIFT_CV (bool), ASP_GATE_SEAM_ENTROPY_SHIFT_CV_FLOOR (float, 0–10); constant SEAM_ENTROPY_SHIFT_CV_GATE_FLOOR=1.5 in constants/animation.py - 5 tests in TestSeamEntropyShiftCv in test_canvas.py; 5 tests in TestSeamEntropyShiftCvGatePipeline in test_pipeline.py

    §5.101 Pipeline Strip Red Channel CV Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — red-axis per-strip color inconsistency]¶

    Problem: Color normalization can fail along individual color axes. The Red channel (BGR channel 2) is particularly important for anime where red is used for blood, fire, character accents, and warm lighting. When some strips have high mean Red and others have low mean Red, this indicates R-axis normalization failure invisible to luma (weighted combination where B and G can compensate) and hue (which only captures angle not axis magnitude). Orthogonal to §5.94 (Value = max channel, not R specifically), §5.86 (hue angle), §5.90 (saturation purity), §5.97 (median luma, grayscale).

    Implementation: - _strip_red_channel_cv(img, n_strips=8) in canvas.py — CV of mean Red (BGR channel 2) per strip; 0.0 for grayscale or mean_red < 1.0 - _RED_CHANNEL_CV_GATE_ENABLED (default ON) + _RED_CHANNEL_CV_GATE_FLOOR=0.6 in pipeline.py; Stage 11.66; env: ASP_GATE_RED_CHANNEL_CV, ASP_GATE_RED_CHANNEL_CV_FLOOR - Schema: ASP_GATE_RED_CHANNEL_CV (bool), ASP_GATE_RED_CHANNEL_CV_FLOOR (float, 0–10); constant RED_CHANNEL_CV_GATE_FLOOR=0.6 in constants/animation.py - 5 tests in TestStripRedChannelCv in test_canvas.py; 5 tests in TestRedChannelCvGatePipeline in test_pipeline.py

    §5.102 Pipeline Seam Blue Shift CV Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — blue-axis seam normalization artifact detection]¶

    Problem: Blue-channel normalization artifacts are common at seams when anime frames alternate between outdoor sky/water scenes (high Blue) and warm indoor scenes (low Blue). When the absolute Blue channel shift at seams varies widely (high CV), some seams are well-matched in the blue axis while others have large shifts — indicating inconsistent blue-channel correction. Orthogonal to luma step (§5.58/§5.60, weighted average), Value shift (§5.94, max channel), hue (§5.86, angle), saturation (§5.90, purity), seam entropy shift (§5.98).

    Implementation: - _seam_blue_shift_cv(img, n_strips=8, boundary_px=3) in canvas.py — CV of |mean_B_above − mean_B_below| per seam (BGR channel 0); 0.0 for grayscale or mean_shift < 1.0 - _SEAM_BLUE_SHIFT_CV_GATE_ENABLED (default ON) + _SEAM_BLUE_SHIFT_CV_GATE_FLOOR=1.2 in pipeline.py; Stage 11.67; env: ASP_GATE_SEAM_BLUE_SHIFT_CV, ASP_GATE_SEAM_BLUE_SHIFT_CV_FLOOR - Schema: ASP_GATE_SEAM_BLUE_SHIFT_CV (bool), ASP_GATE_SEAM_BLUE_SHIFT_CV_FLOOR (float, 0–10); constant SEAM_BLUE_SHIFT_CV_GATE_FLOOR=1.2 in constants/animation.py - 5 tests in TestSeamBlueShiftCv in test_canvas.py; 5 tests in TestSeamBlueShiftCvGatePipeline in test_pipeline.py

    §5.103 Bench Strip Red Channel CV Comparative Gate ✅ [Priority: Low — bench red-channel-CV parity]¶

    Problem: §5.101 detects strip red-channel inconsistency in the pipeline; benchmark needs a paired comparative gate.

    Implementation: - _RED_CHANNEL_CV_ABS_FLOOR=0.20, _RED_CHANNEL_CV_RATIO=3.0 in bench_anime_stitch.py - Comparative gate §5.103 in run_dataset(): fires when asp_val > 0.20 AND (sim_val < 0.07 OR asp_val > 3.0 × max(sim_val, 0.01)) - Schema: ASP_BENCH_RED_CHANNEL_CV_ABS_FLOOR (float), ASP_BENCH_RED_CHANNEL_CV_RATIO (float) - 5 tests in TestRedChannelCvGateBench in test_bench_metrics.py

    §5.104 Bench Seam Blue Shift CV Comparative Gate ✅ [Priority: Low — bench blue-shift-CV parity]¶

    Problem: §5.102 detects blue-axis seam normalization artifacts in the pipeline; benchmark needs a paired comparative gate.

    Implementation: - _SEAM_BLUE_SHIFT_CV_ABS_FLOOR=0.30, _SEAM_BLUE_SHIFT_CV_RATIO=2.0 in bench_anime_stitch.py - Comparative gate §5.104 in run_dataset(): fires when asp_val > 0.30 AND (sim_val < 0.10 OR asp_val > 2.0 × max(sim_val, 0.01)) - Schema: ASP_BENCH_SEAM_BLUE_SHIFT_CV_ABS_FLOOR (float), ASP_BENCH_SEAM_BLUE_SHIFT_CV_RATIO (float) - 5 tests in TestSeamBlueShiftCvGateBench in test_bench_metrics.py

    §5.105 Pipeline Strip Green Channel CV Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — green-axis per-strip color inconsistency]¶

    Problem: Green channel is the dominant perceptual luminance contributor (≈0.587G), so G-axis normalization failures are common yet invisible to: §5.97 (median luma — grayscale, blends all channels), §5.101 (Red channel — different channel), §5.86 (hue angle — not raw axis magnitude), §5.90 (saturation — purity not per-channel value). High Green CV with low Red/Blue CV pinpoints G-axis-only normalization failure.

    Implementation: - _strip_green_channel_cv(img, n_strips=8) in canvas.py — CV of mean Green (BGR channel 1) per strip; 0.0 for grayscale or mean_green < 1.0 - _GREEN_CHANNEL_CV_GATE_ENABLED (default ON) + _GREEN_CHANNEL_CV_GATE_FLOOR=0.5 in pipeline.py; Stage 11.68; env: ASP_GATE_GREEN_CHANNEL_CV, ASP_GATE_GREEN_CHANNEL_CV_FLOOR - Schema: ASP_GATE_GREEN_CHANNEL_CV (bool), ASP_GATE_GREEN_CHANNEL_CV_FLOOR (float, 0–10); constant GREEN_CHANNEL_CV_GATE_FLOOR=0.5 in constants/animation.py - 5 tests in TestStripGreenChannelCv in test_canvas.py; 5 tests in TestGreenChannelCvGatePipeline in test_pipeline.py

    §5.106 Pipeline Seam Red Shift CV Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — red-axis seam normalization artifact detection]¶

    Problem: Red-axis normalization artifacts are common at seams in anime when frames alternate between warm-lit scenes (high Red) and cool-lit or night scenes (low Red). When the absolute Red shift at seams varies widely, some seams are well-matched while others have large R-axis steps — indicating inconsistent red-channel correction. Orthogonal to: §5.58/§5.60 (luma step — grayscale weighted average), §5.102 (seam blue shift — different channel), §5.86 (hue), §5.90 (saturation), §5.94 (Value = max of all channels).

    Implementation: - _seam_red_shift_cv(img, n_strips=8, boundary_px=3) in canvas.py — CV of |mean_R_above − mean_R_below| per seam (BGR channel 2); 0.0 for grayscale or mean_shift < 1.0 - _SEAM_RED_SHIFT_CV_GATE_ENABLED (default ON) + _SEAM_RED_SHIFT_CV_GATE_FLOOR=1.2 in pipeline.py; Stage 11.69; env: ASP_GATE_SEAM_RED_SHIFT_CV, ASP_GATE_SEAM_RED_SHIFT_CV_FLOOR - Schema: ASP_GATE_SEAM_RED_SHIFT_CV (bool), ASP_GATE_SEAM_RED_SHIFT_CV_FLOOR (float, 0–10); constant SEAM_RED_SHIFT_CV_GATE_FLOOR=1.2 in constants/animation.py - 5 tests in TestSeamRedShiftCv in test_canvas.py; 5 tests in TestSeamRedShiftCvGatePipeline in test_pipeline.py

    §5.107 Bench Strip Green Channel CV Comparative Gate ✅ [Priority: Low — bench green-channel-CV parity]¶

    Problem: §5.105 detects strip green-channel inconsistency in the pipeline; benchmark needs a paired comparative gate.

    §5.108 Bench Seam Red Shift CV Comparative Gate ✅ [Priority: Low — bench red-shift-CV parity]¶

    §5.109 Pipeline Strip Blue Channel CV Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — blue-axis per-strip color inconsistency]¶

    Problem: Blue channel is the dominant perceptual differentiator between warm and cool scenes in anime (sky, water, night scenes vs. indoor warm lighting). Completing the R/G/B per-strip channel CV trilogy: §5.101 (Red), §5.105 (Green), §5.109 (Blue). Orthogonal to all three: §5.97 (median luma — grayscale), §5.86 (hue angle — not raw axis magnitude), §5.90 (saturation — purity), §5.102 (seam blue shift — seam-boundary metric, not strip-mean). Per-strip Blue CV detects frames where B-axis correction was applied at different strength across strips.

    Implementation: - _strip_blue_channel_cv(img, n_strips=8) in canvas.py — CV of mean Blue (BGR channel 0) per strip; 0.0 for grayscale or mean_blue < 1.0 - _BLUE_CHANNEL_CV_GATE_ENABLED (default ON) + _BLUE_CHANNEL_CV_GATE_FLOOR=0.6 in pipeline.py; Stage 11.70; env: ASP_GATE_BLUE_CHANNEL_CV, ASP_GATE_BLUE_CHANNEL_CV_FLOOR - Schema: ASP_GATE_BLUE_CHANNEL_CV (bool), ASP_GATE_BLUE_CHANNEL_CV_FLOOR (float, 0–10); constant BLUE_CHANNEL_CV_GATE_FLOOR=0.6 in constants/animation.py - 5 tests in TestStripBlueChannelCv in test_canvas.py; 5 tests in TestBlueChannelCvGatePipeline in test_pipeline.py

    §5.110 Pipeline Seam Green Shift CV Gate ✅ [Priority: Medium — green-axis seam normalization artifact detection]¶

    Problem: Completing the R/G/B per-seam channel shift CV trilogy: §5.102 (Blue), §5.106 (Red), §5.110 (Green). Green seam shift CV differs from luma (§5.58/§5.60, weighted channel blend) because G-axis artifacts visible at seams with high G-vs-G mismatch may be masked when B/R compensate in the luma formula. Orthogonal to Value shift (§5.94, max channel), hue (§5.86, angle), saturation (§5.90, purity), and seam blue (§5.102) / red shift (§5.106, different channels).

    Implementation: - _seam_green_shift_cv(img, n_strips=8, boundary_px=3) in canvas.py — CV of |mean_G_above − mean_G_below| per seam (BGR channel 1); 0.0 for grayscale or mean_shift < 1.0 - _SEAM_GREEN_SHIFT_CV_GATE_ENABLED (default ON) + _SEAM_GREEN_SHIFT_CV_GATE_FLOOR=1.2 in pipeline.py; Stage 11.71; env: ASP_GATE_SEAM_GREEN_SHIFT_CV, ASP_GATE_SEAM_GREEN_SHIFT_CV_FLOOR - Schema: ASP_GATE_SEAM_GREEN_SHIFT_CV (bool), ASP_GATE_SEAM_GREEN_SHIFT_CV_FLOOR (float, 0–10); constant SEAM_GREEN_SHIFT_CV_GATE_FLOOR=1.2 in constants/animation.py - 5 tests in TestSeamGreenShiftCv in test_canvas.py; 5 tests in TestSeamGreenShiftCvGatePipeline in test_pipeline.py

    §5.112 Bench Seam Green Shift CV Comparative Gate ✅ [Priority: Low — bench green-shift-CV parity]¶

    §5.8 Adaptive dy_cv Ceiling for Large-N Sequences ✅ [Priority: Medium — fallback precision]¶

    Problem: The dy_cv gate uses a fixed _DY_CV_MAX=1.5 regardless of how many frames are in the sequence. With N≥8 frames, step irregularity compounds across more seams — the same dy_cv=1.4 is more damaging with 16 frames than with 4.

    Implementation (shipped S168): - _compute_adaptive_dy_cv_max(n_frames, base_max=1.5) in pipeline.py: returns base_max for N<8; max(base_max × 8/N, 0.8) for N≥8 - Scale: N=8→1.5, N=16→0.8 (floor), N=100→0.8 (floor). Custom base respected. - DY_CV_ADAPTIVE_FLOOR: float = 0.8 in constants/animation.py - _compute_adaptive_dy_cv_max exported in __all__ - 5 tests in TestAdaptiveDyCvMax (test_pipeline.py)

Session 106 complete: §1.42 Linear Interpolation Bg Fill. _linear_interp_zero_bg(canvas, zero_mask) → np.ndarray added to bg_complete.py — for each column, iterates unknown (zero-coverage) rows and checks for known pixels both above and below; when both boundaries exist, fills with a per-channel linear blend (1−t) × pixel_above + t × pixel_below where t = (r − r_above) / (r_below − r_above); when only one boundary exists (top/bottom edge gaps), falls back to nearest-neighbour copy so no pixel is left unfilled. _linear_interp_zero_bg added to __all__. Wired in complete_background() between ProPainter and _nn_fill_zero_bg branches: when _INTERP_BG_FILL is set, uses linear interpolation instead of NN copy. Rationale: _nn_fill_zero_bg already picks the correct nearest neighbour bidirectionally, but hard-copies it — producing a discrete color step at the midpoint when the pixel above and below differ (e.g., background transitions from light sky at top to dark floor at bottom across a large gap). Linear interpolation removes this step artefact at negligible extra cost. _INTERP_BG_FILL bool module flag (default OFF; ASP_INTERP_BG_FILL=1). Session 105 complete: §1.41 Sequential Gain Chain-Drift Guard. _check_gain_chain_drift(gains: np.ndarray, max_ratio: float) → bool added to rendering.py — computes the per-channel cumulative product of the gains array (np.prod(gains, axis=0), shape (3,)) and returns True when |log(cum_c)| > log(max_ratio) for any channel c. The sequential correction in _compute_sequential_color_gains chains N per-pair photometric corrections: if each pair nudges in the same direction (e.g., monotonically dimming video capture), the total effect by frame N can be an implausible 3–7× brightness shift. Rather than apply a systematically drifted correction that would make the canvas worse than no correction, the guard resets all gains to 1.0 and biases to 0.0 when drift is detected. Called with _GAIN_DRIFT_MAX after the main computation loop. _GAIN_DRIFT_MAX float module flag (default 0.0=off; ASP_GAIN_DRIFT_MAX=2.0 recommended). GAIN_DRIFT_MAX=2.0 in constants/animation.py. Session 102 complete: §1.38 LoFTR Background Match Ratio Gate. _compute_bg_match_ratio(n_bg_pts: int, n_total_pts: int) → float added to matching.py — returns float(n_bg_pts) / max(1, n_total_pts); 0.0 when n_total_pts == 0 (no ZeroDivisionError). Session 100 complete: §1.36 LoFTR Translation Consensus Spread Filter. _compute_translation_spread(pts_i, pts_j) → (mad_dx, mad_dy) added to matching.py — computes the Median Absolute Deviation of per-match displacement estimates around their median (dx, dy). Session 93 complete: §2.14 Triangular Consistency Filter. _triangular_consistency_filter(edges, max_residual_px) → List[Dict] in pipeline.py — iterates all triangles (i→j, j→k, i→k) in edge graph; computes L2 residual between predicted (leg-sum) and observed (hypotenuse) displacement; penalises weakest edge (weight × 0.5) when residual > threshold; preserves edge for BA at reduced trust (halving, not dropping).
